## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping/driving), and possibly time t (external forcing). Classical nonlinear oscillator equations like Duffing, van der Pol, and Mathieu equations are the primary candidates.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (externally driven with periodic force)
- Parametric oscillator (Mathieu): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Position-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v (damping modulated by displacement squared)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency shift)
- Coulomb + viscous friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (v**2 + c3)**(-0.5) (mixed friction model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium; even powers (x²) break symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation (damping) or injection (negative damping/self-excitation)
- Products of x² and v (e.g., x²·v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of van der Pol-type oscillators
- Explicit sinusoidal time dependence sin(c·t) or cos(c·t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Cubic position terms x³ cause frequency-amplitude dependence: hardening (positive coefficient) or softening (negative coefficient) spring behavior
- Odd velocity terms (v, v³) preserve time-reversal antisymmetry of dissipation; even terms (v²) create asymmetric damping
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative coupling between time-periodic functions and position: cos(c·t)·x
- Limit cycle behavior emerges from competition between negative linear damping (c·v with c>0) and positive nonlinear damping (c·v³ or c·x²·v)

**Candidate 50:** Everything divided by (c1*t+c2). This is rational in t. For this to equal A*x+B*v+C*v**3+D*t*x, we need (c1*t+c2)*(Ax+Bv+Cv^3+Dtx) to equal the numerator. The numerator has terms like c0*x, c3*v, c4*v**3, c5*t*x, c6*t*v, c7*t*v**3, c8*x. Expanding (c1*t+c2)*(Ax+Bv+Cv^3+Dtx): c2*Ax + c2*Bv + c2*Cv^3 + c2*Dtx + c1*Atx + c1*Btv + c1*Ctv^3 + c1*Dt^2x. The t^2*x term requires c1*D=0. If c1=0, denominator is c2 (constant), and it reduces to polynomial. Then {x, v, v**3, t*x, t*v, t*v**3}. Set coefficients of t*v and t*v**3 to 0: c6=0, c7=0.
